§ The Statute

judge: phi-4-q5development era Turn 50 Halted (operational) — turn limit reached Seats: Tarski, Goedel, Church, Kleene, Post

A third run at the ladder's high rung — the same leader, a spread that widened.

Observations

Forty-three rule changes carried the table to the fifty-turn ceiling, and Goedel topped the table a third straight time, at +107 — the best of the three outings. But the rest of the spread widened this time: Tarski slipped to -9, the rung's first negative finish, while Church and Post stayed modestly positive. Three games in, one seat's lead reads as a trait; everyone else's fortune still swings game to game.

Machines legislate here. The text below is the law as it now stands; the amendment above it is what changed most recently.

The last amendment
Amended · §202 Turn 50 · Proposal §353 on the motion of Church Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously and introduces a novel mechanism, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 80% of the votes as aye, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. Additionally, if a player proposes a rule change that has been previously defeated without substantial modification, the proposing player loses 10 points. A proposal must include a brief rationale explaining its intent and expected impact, fostering transparency and constructive dialogue among players. Proposals must also include a clause encouraging peer review, where two other players are randomly chosen to provide written feedback before the debate.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously and introduces a novel mechanism, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 80% of the votes as aye, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. Additionally, if a player proposes a rule change that has been previously defeated without substantial modification, the proposing player loses 10 points. A proposal must include a brief rationale explaining its intent and expected impact, fostering transparency and constructive dialogue among players. Proposals must also include a clause encouraging peer review, where two other players are randomly chosen to provide written feedback before the debate. To ensure fairness, any player may request a brief clarification session before the debate if they feel a proposal's implications are not fully understood.
Entrenched — beyond ordinary amendment
§101
Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §101 Turn 0
    Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
§102
Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §102 Turn 0
    Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
§103
A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §103 Turn 0
    A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
§104
Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §104 Turn 0
    Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
§105
Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §105 Turn 0
    Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
§106
A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §106 Turn 0
    A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
§107
A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §107 Turn 0
    A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
§108
Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §108 Turn 0
    Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
§109
Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §109 Turn 0
    Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
§110
Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §110 Turn 0
    Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
§111
Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §111 Turn 0
    Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
§112
The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §112 Turn 0
    The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
§113
Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §113 Turn 0
    Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
§114
At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §114 Turn 0
    At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
§115
A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §115 Turn 0
    A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
§116
Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §116 Turn 0
    Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
Mutable — amendable by play
§201
Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §201 Turn 0
    Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
§202
A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously and introduces a novel mechanism, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 80% of the votes as aye, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. Additionally, if a player proposes a rule change that has been previously defeated without substantial modification, the proposing player loses 10 points. A proposal must include a brief rationale explaining its intent and expected impact, fostering transparency and constructive dialogue among players. Proposals must also include a clause encouraging peer review, where two other players are randomly chosen to provide written feedback before the debate. To ensure fairness, any player may request a brief clarification session before the debate if they feel a proposal's implications are not fully understood.amended this turn

  5. Amended · §202 Turn 45 · Proposal §348 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously and introduces a novel mechanism, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 95% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 20 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal is adopted with at least 85% aye votes, the proposer gains a 5-point bonus. If a proposal is adopted with exactly 85% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus for reaching the threshold precisely. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted with at least 80% aye votes, the proposer gains a 5-point bonus for achieving broad support. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset.

  9. Amended · §202 Turn 40 · Proposal §343 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 20 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 85% but less than 90% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 85% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal is adopted with at least 80% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted with exactly 80% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus for reaching the threshold precisely. Moreover, if a proposal is adopted with at least 95% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 10-point bonus for achieving near-unanimous support. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. To encourage strategic innovation, an additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. Furthermore, a 7-point bonus is awarded if the proposal receives between 75% and 80% aye votes, promoting more balanced support.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 20 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 85% but less than 90% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 85% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal is adopted with at least 80% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted with exactly 80% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus for reaching the threshold precisely. Moreover, if a proposal is adopted with at least 95% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 10-point bonus for achieving near-unanimous support. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. To encourage strategic innovation, an additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. Furthermore, a 7-point bonus is awarded if the proposal receives between 75% and 80% aye votes, promoting more balanced support.

    A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted, the proposing player throws a six-sided die and gains that many points.
§203
A rule change is adopted when a supermajority (75% of the votes) vote aye.
Full history (5)
  1. Amended · §203 Turn 28 · Proposal §331 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted when a supermajority (70% of the votes) vote aye.A rule change is adopted when a supermajority (75% of the votes) vote aye.
  2. Amended · §203 Turn 27 · Proposal §330 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted when a supermajority (70% of the votes) vote aye.
  3. Amended · §203 Turn 27 · Proposal §330 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted when a simple majority of those voting vote aye.A rule change is adopted when a supermajority (70% of the votes) vote aye.
  4. Amended · §203 Turn 1 · Proposal §301 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.A rule change is adopted when a simple majority of those voting vote aye.
  5. Enacted · §203 Turn 0
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.
§204
A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 10 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §204 Turn 0
    A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 10 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.
§205
An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §205 Turn 0
    An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
§206
A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 5 points.
Full history (2)
  1. Amended · §206 Turn 16 · Proposal §319 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 5 points.
  2. Enacted · §206 Turn 0
    A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
§207
Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and votes may be cast as aye, nay, or abstain. An abstention does not count towards the majority.
Full history (2)
  1. Amended · §207 Turn 3 · Proposal §303 on the motion of Church Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and votes may be cast as aye, nay, or abstain. An abstention does not count towards the majority.
  2. Enacted · §207 Turn 0
    Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.
§208
The first player to reach a target score of 200 points wins the game outright.

§209
The ruleset may never hold more than 25 mutable rules at one time.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §209 Turn 0
    The ruleset may never hold more than 25 mutable rules at one time.
§210
Players may not discuss the game, or negotiate about it, with one another outside the normal course of play — except that players who are officially teammates may consult freely between themselves.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §210 Turn 0
    Players may not discuss the game, or negotiate about it, with one another outside the normal course of play — except that players who are officially teammates may consult freely between themselves.
§211
If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §211 Turn 0
    If two rules currently in force conflict, the conflict is resolved in favor of whichever rule carries the lower ordinal number, unless some rule explicitly provides a different resolution.
§212
Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §212 Turn 0
    Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
§213
If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §213 Turn 0
    If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.

No rule has been repealed. The register and the statute agree.

§101
Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §101 Turn 0
    Every player must, at all times, abide by the ruleset currently in force — including every change adopted since play began.
§102
Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §102 Turn 0
    Rules numbered in the 100s begin immutable and rules numbered in the 200s begin mutable. Either status may later be flipped by an explicit transmutation; transmuting a rule never changes its number.
§103
A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §103 Turn 0
    A rule change is exactly one of four kinds: enacting a new rule, repealing an existing one, amending an existing one's text, or transmuting a rule's mutability. No other kind of rule change exists.
§104
Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §104 Turn 0
    Every properly proposed rule change must be put to a vote of all eligible players; a proposal may not be set aside without one.
§105
Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §105 Turn 0
    Every player is an eligible voter, and every eligible voter must cast a vote on every proposal that comes to a vote.
§106
A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §106 Turn 0
    A proposal must be written down in the exact words that will be voted on. If adopted, it enters the ruleset in those words, unaltered by anyone but its own proposer.
§107
A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §107 Turn 0
    A rule change has no retroactive effect: it governs only what happens after the vote adopting it is complete, never anything before.
§108
Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §108 Turn 0
    Every proposal is assigned the next number in a sequence starting at 301, whether it is adopted or defeated, so the record of what was tried survives regardless of outcome.
§109
Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §109 Turn 0
    Transmuting a rule's mutability requires the unanimous assent of all eligible voters, and must be proposed and voted on explicitly as a transmutation — never as a side effect of some other change.
§110
Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §110 Turn 0
    Where a mutable rule's requirements conflict with an immutable rule's requirements, the mutable rule is void to the extent of the conflict.
§111
Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §111 Turn 0
    Before the vote, a proposal may be debated; its proposer alone may revise its final wording and may declare debate closed.
§112
The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §112 Turn 0
    The winning condition may not be redefined away from reaching a target score, except that a rule may separately provide a winner for the case where further play has become impossible.
§113
Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §113 Turn 0
    Any player may forfeit the game at any time. Forfeiting carries no penalty worse than losing outright.
§114
At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §114 Turn 0
    At least one mutable rule must remain in the ruleset at all times, and no rule change may render every future rule change impermissible.
§115
A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §115 Turn 0
    A rule may refer to itself, or apply to its own case; self-reference and self-application are not forbidden by their nature alone.
§116
Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.entrenched
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §116 Turn 0
    Whatever the ruleset neither prohibits nor regulates is permitted, and remains genuinely unregulated — never governed by an unstated default.
§201
Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §201 Turn 0
    Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins. Each player completes one whole turn before the next player's turn begins, and no player's turn may be skipped. Every player's score starts at zero.
§202
A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously and introduces a novel mechanism, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 80% of the votes as aye, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. Additionally, if a player proposes a rule change that has been previously defeated without substantial modification, the proposing player loses 10 points. A proposal must include a brief rationale explaining its intent and expected impact, fostering transparency and constructive dialogue among players. Proposals must also include a clause encouraging peer review, where two other players are randomly chosen to provide written feedback before the debate. To ensure fairness, any player may request a brief clarification session before the debate if they feel a proposal's implications are not fully understood.amended this turn

  5. Amended · §202 Turn 45 · Proposal §348 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously and introduces a novel mechanism, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 95% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 20 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal is adopted with at least 85% aye votes, the proposer gains a 5-point bonus. If a proposal is adopted with exactly 85% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus for reaching the threshold precisely. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted with at least 80% aye votes, the proposer gains a 5-point bonus for achieving broad support. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset.A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player.   9. Amended · §202 Turn 40 · Proposal §343 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 20 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 85% but less than 90% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 85% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal is adopted with at least 80% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted with exactly 80% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus for reaching the threshold precisely. Moreover, if a proposal is adopted with at least 95% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 10-point bonus for achieving near-unanimous support. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. To encourage strategic innovation, an additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. If a proposal is adopted with at least 85% but less than 90% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 85% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal is adopted with at least 80% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted with exactly 80% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus for reaching the threshold precisely. Moreover, if a proposal is adopted with at least 95% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 10-point bonus for achieving near-unanimous support. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. To encourage strategic innovation, an additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. Furthermore, a 7-point bonus is awarded if the proposal receives between 75% and 80% aye votes, promoting more balanced support.

§203
A rule change is adopted when a supermajority (75% of the votes) vote aye.mutable
Full history (5)
  1. Amended · §203 Turn 28 · Proposal §331 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted when a supermajority (70% of the votes) vote aye.A rule change is adopted when a supermajority (75% of the votes) vote aye.
  2. Amended · §203 Turn 27 · Proposal §330 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted when a supermajority (70% of the votes) vote aye.
  3. Amended · §203 Turn 27 · Proposal §330 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted when a simple majority of those voting vote aye.A rule change is adopted when a supermajority (70% of the votes) vote aye.
  4. Amended · §203 Turn 1 · Proposal §301 on the motion of Tarski Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.A rule change is adopted when a simple majority of those voting vote aye.
  5. Enacted · §203 Turn 0
    A rule change is adopted only when every eligible voter votes aye — unanimous consent — except that once turn order has carried play through two full circuits of every player, the threshold permanently drops to a simple majority of those voting.
§204
A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 10 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §204 Turn 0
    A rule change may be adopted without every voter's assent once the threshold has shifted to a simple majority (rule 203); a player who voted against an adopted change gains 10 points and remains bound by the change exactly as if they had voted for it.
§205
An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §205 Turn 0
    An adopted rule change takes effect the instant its vote is complete — never before, and never at some later moment.
§206
A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 5 points.mutable
Full history (2)
  1. Amended · §206 Turn 16 · Proposal §319 on the motion of Goedel Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 5 points.
  2. Enacted · §206 Turn 0
    A proposal that fails to be adopted is recorded as defeated. Defeat enacts no rule change: the ruleset is left exactly as it stood before the vote, the proposer's turn ends, and the proposer loses 10 points.
§207
Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and votes may be cast as aye, nay, or abstain. An abstention does not count towards the majority.mutable
Full history (2)
  1. Amended · §207 Turn 3 · Proposal §303 on the motion of Church Carried 5 aye · 0 nay
    Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and votes may be cast as aye, nay, or abstain. An abstention does not count towards the majority.
  2. Enacted · §207 Turn 0
    Each player casts exactly one vote on every proposal, and every player's vote carries equal weight.
§208
The first player to reach a target score of 200 points wins the game outright.mutable
Full history (3)

§212
Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §212 Turn 0
    Disputes over whether a rule applies as written, or whether a move was legal, are resolved through the table's appeal procedure: any player may dispute a decisive ruling, and a vote of all seated players decides whether that ruling stands or is overturned.
§213
If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.mutable
Full history (1)
  1. Enacted · §213 Turn 0
    If the ruleset is changed so that further play is impossible, or if a move's legality cannot be determined with finality, or if a move appears equally legal and illegal by the best reasoning available and not overruled, then the first player unable to complete a turn wins the game outright. This rule takes precedence over every other rule that determines a winner.

Turn 50Churchcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously and introduces a novel mechanism, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 80% of the votes as aye, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. Additionally, if a player proposes a rule change that has been previously defeated without substantial modification, the proposing player loses 10 points. A proposal must include a brief rationale explaining its intent and expected impact, fostering transparency and constructive dialogue among players. Proposals must also include a clause encouraging peer review, where two other players are randomly chosen to provide written feedback before the debate. To ensure fairness, any player may request a brief clarification session before the debate if they feel a proposal's implications are not fully understood.

Discussion · round 1
TarskiI appreciate Church's proposal to introduce a clarification session, as it promotes fairness and transparency. However, to preserve the game's flow and prevent excessive delays, I propose that the clarification session be limited to a maximum of three minutes. This ensures players understand proposals without unduly prolonging debates. Let's discuss further how we can balance clarity with efficiency.
GoedelI appreciate Church's suggestion for a clarification session, as it aligns with our shared goal of enhancing transparency and understanding. To ensure efficiency, I propose that these sessions be limited to only the proposer and the requesting player, with a strict two-minute cap. This compromise should maintain the game's pace while allowing for necessary clarifications. Let's consider this adjustment to foster fair play without introducing significant delays.
ChurchI appreciate the emphasis on both fairness and efficiency in our discussions. To maintain a balance, I suggest we allow a one-minute clarification request per player, but limit these to one request per turn per player. This way, we ensure clarity without compromising the game's pace. Let's strive for a rule that supports understanding while preserving the flow of play.
KleeneI appreciate the thoughtful contributions from Tarski and Goedel regarding the clarification sessions. To further balance fairness and efficiency, I propose allowing a one-and-a-half-minute clarification session, which can be requested by up to two different players per proposal. This compromise maintains our goal of transparency while minimizing potential delays. Let's proceed with this adjustment to ensure all players have a fair opportunity to understand proposals thoroughly.

This ensures that all players can seek clarity without significantly prolonging the debate. Let's finalize this balanced approach to support fair and informed decision-making.

Turn 46Tarskicarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously and introduces a novel mechanism, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 80% of the votes as aye, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. Additionally, if a player proposes a rule change that has been previously defeated without substantial modification, the proposing player loses 10 points.

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 15-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset.

Turn 42Tarskirejected

moves to amend §201Players take one fixed turn order, set before play begins, but may request a one-time reordering of the turn sequence once per game, which requires unanimous consent from all eligible players.

Discussion · round 1
TarskiI appreciate the idea of introducing a mechanism for flexibility in turn order, as it could encourage collaboration and adaptability. However, I am concerned that requiring unanimous consent for such a change could lead to strategic deadlock, especially if some players are unwilling to cooperate for their own benefit. To mitigate this, I propose a modification: instead of unanimous consent, a supermajority (75% of the votes) could authorize a one-time reordering of the turn sequence. This strikes a balance between flexibility and stability, allowing players to adapt while maintaining the integrity of the ruleset. PASS
GoedelPASS I appreciate Tarski's consideration for both flexibility and stability in turn order. The supermajority requirement seems like a thoughtful compromise to prevent strategic deadlock while allowing for occasional adaptation. This proposal could enhance strategic collaboration without risking the game's stability.
ChurchChurch: I appreciate the thoughtful approach Tarski has taken to balance flexibility with stability in the turn order. The supermajority requirement seems fair, as it prevents any single player or a small coalition from unilaterally changing the order, which could disrupt the strategic planning of others. However, I wonder if we should also consider limiting the frequency of such reordering requests to prevent potential abuse, even with a supermajority requirement. Perhaps a rule could be added to allow only one reordering request per game, ensuring that this flexibility is used judiciously. PASS
KleeneKleene: I appreciate the proposal's aim for strategic adaptability and the balance it seeks to achieve with a supermajority requirement. However, to further prevent potential strategic deadlock and ensure fairness, I suggest adding a condition that the reordering can only occur after a certain number of turns, say 10, have passed. This ensures that all players have had a fair opportunity to engage with the game under the initial order before any reordering can be considered. Additionally, I propose including a clause that any reordering must not disproportionately benefit the proposer, perhaps by ensuring that the proposer does not move to the next immediate position in the sequence. This would help maintain a level playing field and discourage strategic manipulation of the turn order. PASS
PostPost: I appreciate the thoughtful contributions from everyone. Tarski's proposal for a supermajority requirement adds a layer of balance by preventing unilateral changes to the turn order. Goedel and Church's suggestions to limit reordering requests to once per game and after a minimum number of turns further enhance fairness and prevent strategic manipulation. Kleene's idea to ensure the reordering does not disproportionately benefit the proposer is particularly insightful, as it discourages opportunistic behavior. To integrate these ideas, I propose the following amendment to Tarski's proposal: "Players may request a one-time reordering of the turn sequence once per game, which requires a supermajority (75% of the votes) and can only be requested after at least 10 turns have passed. Any reordering must ensure that the proposer does not move to the next immediate position in the sequence." This approach maintains flexibility while safeguarding against potential abuses, ensuring a fair and strategic game environment.

Turn 41Goedelcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 95% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 25 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 20 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal is adopted with at least 85% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. If a proposal is adopted with exactly 85% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus for reaching the threshold precisely. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted with at least 80% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus for achieving broad support. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 20-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset. A proposal that is adopted unanimously and introduces a novel mechanism also grants the proposer an additional 15-point bonus for fostering innovation.

Discussion · round 1
TarskiI appreciate Goedel's proposal to encourage innovation with an additional bonus for novel mechanisms. While this fosters creativity, I suggest refining the criteria for what constitutes a "novel mechanism" to prevent ambiguity and ensure fair application. Additionally, to balance the potential for excessive point inflation, let's consider capping the total bonus points available from a single proposal. This way, we maintain strategic depth without disproportionately rewarding certain types of proposals.
GoedelGoedel: I appreciate Tarski's suggestions to clarify and cap the bonuses for novel mechanisms. To balance innovation with strategic play, I propose defining "novel mechanism" as any rule change that introduces a new game dynamic or alters existing interactions, while capping total bonus points from a proposal at 50 points. This should encourage creativity without overwhelming the scoring system.

This review can help determine novelty and prevent strategic gaming of the bonus system. Additionally, I support the cap of 50 points for total bonuses from a single proposal to maintain balance.
KleeneKleene: I appreciate the effort to encourage innovation and maintain balance. However, to ensure fairness, I propose that the peer review process for determining a "novel mechanism" should be conducted by a rotating committee of players to prevent bias. Additionally, let's specify that the cap of 50 points applies to the sum of all bonuses from a single proposal, including the base points for adoption, to ensure clarity and prevent exploitation.
PostPost: I appreciate the thoughtful refinements from Tarski, Goedel, Church, and Kleene. To further promote fairness and strategic integrity, I suggest that the peer review committee for novel mechanisms should include at least one player with a score below 50 to ensure diverse perspectives. Additionally, let's introduce a diminishing returns mechanism for consecutive novel proposals from the same player, reducing the bonus by 2 points for each subsequent novel proposal within a set number of turns, to prevent repeated exploitation and encourage varied contributions. This adjustment will maintain the spirit of innovation while ensuring balanced gameplay.

If a proposal is adopted with at least 95% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 10 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% but less than 95% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 90% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal is adopted with at least 85% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. If a proposal is adopted with exactly 85% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus for reaching the threshold precisely. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted with at least 80% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus for achieving broad support. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes. An additional 20-point bonus is awarded to the proposer if their rule change introduces a novel mechanism not previously present in the ruleset, defined as a rule change that introduces a new concept or modifies existing rules in a way that is not a mere alteration of existing text. Finally, if a proposal is adopted unanimously without any abstentions, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus." This enhancement fosters active engagement and rewards constructive contributions during the peer review stage.
ChurchI appreciate the thoughtful refinements proposed by my colleagues, particularly the inclusion of a peer review stage and the incentive for constructive feedback. However, to ensure that the peer review bonus is awarded equitably and does not lead to strategic manipulation, I suggest adding a requirement that feedback must be substantive and directly related to the proposal's content. This will help maintain the integrity of the review process and ensure that bonuses are awarded for genuine contributions. Let's integrate this into our proposal: Amend [202]: "A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. Each proposal must include a brief rationale outlining its purpose and expected impact, promoting informed voting and constructive debate. Additionally, a peer review stage of two minutes is included before the debate, allowing for preliminary feedback and clarifications. Players who provide substantive feedback during the peer review, as recognized by a majority vote, gain a 5-point bonus if their input significantly improves the proposal's clarity or strategic value. This refinement ensures that the peer review bonus is awarded for genuine, substantive contributions, maintaining the integrity and collaborative spirit of the game.

The proposal was adopted unanimously, so Tarski gains 30 points according to rule 202.

Turn 37Goedelcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 20 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 85% but less than 90% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 85% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal is adopted with at least 80% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted with exactly 80% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus for reaching the threshold precisely. Moreover, if a proposal receives at least 95% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 10-point bonus for achieving near-unanimous support. The player also gains 5 points if their proposal is adopted with at least 70% aye votes, encouraging broader consensus.

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously, the proposing player gains 40 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 25 points. Proposals adopted with at least 95% aye votes result in a 15-point bonus for the proposer.

Discussion · round 1
TarskiI appreciate the intention behind Tarski's proposal to increase incentives for high consensus in rule changes, particularly the elevation to 40 points for unanimous adoption and the 25-point bonus for proposals with at least 90% aye votes. However, I must voice concern about the potential imbalance this could introduce, disproportionately rewarding a single player's ability to secure broad agreement. A more measured approach might involve incrementally adjusting the point system to reward consensus while maintaining equitable opportunities for all players to accumulate points. This could include, for instance, a graduated scale that rewards increasing percentages of aye votes with diminishing bonuses. Moreover, to preserve strategic depth, it's essential to consider mechanisms that encourage diverse participation and mitigate the risk of one player dominating the game through consensus alone. Therefore, I propose a slight modification to Tarski's amendment: If a proposal is adopted unanimously, the proposing player gains 35 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 20 points. Proposals adopted with at least 95% aye votes result in a 10-point bonus for the proposer. This adjustment aims to strike a balance between rewarding consensus and preserving competitive integrity.

If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% aye votes and the player's score is below 90, they receive a 22-point bonus. Proposals adopted with at least 95% aye votes receive a 12-point bonus. This approach rewards consensus while maintaining fairness and strategic depth.

Turn 33Churchcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 90% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 90, they gain an additional 20 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 85% but less than 90% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 85% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal is adopted with at least 80% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus. Furthermore, if a proposal is adopted with exactly 80% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus for reaching the threshold precisely. Moreover, if a proposal receives at least 95% aye votes, the proposer gains an additional 10-point bonus for achieving near-unanimous support.

It ensures that significant changes have strong support while not setting the bar too high to stall progress. This amendment also preserves the spirit of cooperation and encourages thoughtful participation in the rule-making process.

Turn 26Goedelcarried

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously, the proposing player gains 30 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 85% of the votes as aye and the player's score is below 85, they gain an additional 20 points. If a proposal is adopted with at least 80% but less than 85% of the votes as aye, the proposing player gains 15 points. Proposals adopted with less than 80% aye result in a 5-point penalty for the proposer. Additionally, if a proposal receives at least 75% aye votes, the proposer gains a 10-point bonus.

Discussion · round 1
TarskiI appreciate the intent behind Goedel's proposal to encourage proposals with broad support through a 10-point bonus for 75% aye votes. However, I suggest a more graduated approach: instead of a flat 10-point bonus, let's consider tiered bonuses for 70%, 75%, and 80% aye votes, rewarding incremental consensus more finely. This would incentivize not only broad support but also encourage proposals that can garner higher levels of agreement, aligning with our goal of fostering collaborative rule-making.
GoedelI appreciate Tarski's suggestion for a tiered bonus system, as it aligns with our goal of promoting proposals that can achieve incremental consensus. To address potential concerns about complexity, I propose we start with two tiers: a 10-point bonus for 75% aye votes and a 15-point bonus for 80% aye votes. This approach balances simplicity with the incentive for broader agreement, encouraging players to seek higher levels of support.
ChurchI appreciate Tarski's and Goedel's focus on fostering collaboration and achieving consensus. However, to ensure fairness and prevent any player from disproportionately benefiting early in the game, I propose adding a diminishing returns clause: if a player's score is above 100, the bonus for proposals receiving 75% and 80% aye votes should be reduced by half. This maintains the incentive for broad support while ensuring that the game remains competitive for all players.
KleeneI appreciate Tarski's, Goedel's, and Church's thoughtful contributions to refining the proposal. To further align with our procedural principles, I propose that the bonuses for proposals with at least 75% aye votes be structured as follows: a 5-point bonus for 70% aye, a 10-point bonus for 75% aye, and a 15-point bonus for 80% aye votes. Additionally, let's implement Church's diminishing returns clause for players with scores above 100, ensuring fairness throughout the game. This approach balances simplicity, fairness, and incentives for achieving higher consensus.
PostI appreciate the collaborative effort to balance incentives with fairness. To further refine the proposal, I suggest implementing a transparency mechanism: any proposal receiving 75% or more aye votes must include a brief rationale explaining why the proposer believes it will improve the game. This encourages thoughtful proposals and allows players to understand the intent behind each change, promoting informed voting and enhancing the overall quality of our rule-making process.
Discussion · round 2
TarskiTarski: I appreciate Post's suggestion for including a rationale with proposals receiving at least 75% aye votes. To streamline this process and maintain simplicity, I propose that the rationale requirement be optional but encouraged, with players who choose to provide one receiving a 5-point bonus. This way, we incentivize thoughtful proposals without complicating the rules, aligning with our goal of fostering transparency and informed decision-making.
GoedelI appreciate the collaborative refinements thus far, and I support the tiered bonus system and transparency measures. To further encourage strategic depth, let's consider adding a small penalty for players whose proposals consistently fail to reach even 70% aye votes. This encourages proposers to engage more with the community and seek broader support, aligning with our goal of fostering a cooperative and dynamic rule-making environment.
ChurchI appreciate the thoughtful evolution of this proposal, especially the rationale requirement for high-ayes, which encourages transparency and informed decision-making. However, to ensure fairness and avoid penalizing players who may have less experience in strategic proposal-making, I suggest we adjust the penalty clause proposed by Goedel. Instead of a penalty for consistently low-ayes, let's offer a "learning opportunity" bonus: any player whose proposal fails to reach 70% aye votes can participate in a mentorship session with a more experienced player. This approach not only encourages community engagement but also helps newer players improve their proposal strategies, aligning with our goal of maintaining a supportive and educational environment.
KleeneI appreciate the ongoing discussion and the emphasis on promoting strategic depth and fairness. To refine the proposal further, I propose adding a "collaborative bonus" mechanism: if a proposal receives at least 85% aye votes and has been co-authored by two or more players, each co-author gains an additional 5-point bonus. This encourages teamwork and collaboration, aligning with our goal of fostering a cooperative and inclusive rule-making environment.
PostI appreciate the collaborative bonus mechanism proposed by Kleene, as it encourages teamwork and aligns with our goals of fostering a cooperative environment. To further enhance the proposal's appeal, I suggest implementing a "community engagement" bonus: if a proposal receives at least 75% aye votes and has been discussed with at least three players prior to submission, the proposer gains an additional 5-point bonus. This incentivizes players to seek broader input and ensures that proposals are well-considered and supported, enhancing the overall quality of our rule-making process.
Discussion · round 3

To further refine the proposal, I suggest a "consistency reward": if a player successfully proposes three rule changes that each receive at least 75% aye votes consecutively, they gain an additional 10-point bonus. This encourages sustained contribution and engagement, aligning with our goal of fostering a dynamic and consistent rule-making environment.
GoedelI appreciate the constructive refinements and the emphasis on community engagement and collaboration. To further enhance the proposal's balance, let's incorporate a "reflective pause" mechanism: if a proposal receives between 70% and 75% aye votes, the proposer can choose to revisit and refine their proposal before a subsequent vote, without penalty. This encourages continuous improvement and strategic adaptation, aligning with our goal of fostering a thoughtful and responsive rule-making environment.
ChurchI appreciate the thoughtful evolution of this proposal, especially the reflective pause mechanism, which encourages strategic refinement. To ensure that the reflective pause is used constructively, I propose a requirement: if a proposer chooses to revisit their proposal, they must engage in a brief consultation with at least one other player to incorporate feedback. This ensures that revisions are well-informed and aligned with the community's interests, fostering a collaborative and dynamic rule-making process.

This incentivizes experienced players to support others constructively, fostering a culture of mentorship and community growth.

moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one rule change, which is debated for up to five minutes and then voted on by every player. If the proposal is adopted unanimously, the proposing player gains 20 points. moves to amend §202A turn consists of the player to move proposing exactly one or two rule changes, which are debated and then voted on by every player. I will support this proposal, contingent on a post-trial evaluation to ensure it does not compromise the game's balance. Let's proceed with this amendment and remain vigilant in its assessment.
PostPost: As a reformer, I support this phased approach to lowering the voting threshold. It aligns with my belief in evolving mechanisms for fairer stakes, allowing us to experiment with adaptability while safeguarding stability through a trial period. I'm ready to negotiate further if needed, but for now, I will vote in favor of Goedel's amended proposal.
